data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Create an AWS Lambda function which sends emails when it finds misconfigured Amazon RDS databases</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-correct--PLOEU" data-purpose="answer"><div><span data-purpose="answer-result-header-user-label" class="result-pane--answer-by-user-label--PSH86 ud-heading-xs" style="background: oklch(0.8101 0.0873 162.22); color: oklch(0.3072 0.0555 158.67);">Correct answer</span></div><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.2565 0.0265 278.04);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Use AWS CloudFormation to manage Amazon RDS databases</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Attach an IAM policy to interns preventing them from creating an Amazon RDS database</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Store your recommendations in a custom AWS Trusted Advisor rule</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-related-fields--c3m--"><div class="overall-explanation-pane--overall-explanation--G-hLQ ud-form-group"><label class="ud-heading-md ud-form-label ud-heading-sm" for="form-group--1081">Overall explanation</label><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-text-md rt-scaffolding" id="overall-explanation"><p>Correct option:</p>

<p><strong>Use AWS CloudFormation to manage Amazon RDS databases</strong></p>

<p>AWS CloudFormation provides a common language for you to model and provision AWS and third-party application resources in your cloud environment. AWS CloudFormation allows you to use programming languages or a simple text file to model and provision, in an automated and secure manner, all the resources needed for your applications across all regions and accounts. This gives you a single source of truth for your AWS and third-party resources.</p>

<p>AWS CloudFormation allows you to keep your infrastructure as code and re-use the best practices around your company for configuration parameters. Therefore, this is the correct option for the given use-case.</p>

<p>Incorrect options:</p>

<p><strong>Store your recommendations in a custom AWS Trusted Advisor rule</strong> - AWS Trusted Advisor is an online tool that provides you real-time guidance to help you provision your resources following AWS best practices. Whether establishing new workflows, developing applications, or as part of ongoing improvement, take advantage of the recommendations provided by AWS Trusted Advisor regularly to help keep your solutions provisioned optimally. AWS Trusted Advisor just provides recommendations rather than creating reusable infrastructure templates.</p>

<p><strong>Create an AWS Lambda function which sends emails when it finds misconfigured Amazon RDS databases</strong> - Using an AWS Lambda function to scan for a misconfigured Amazon RDS database is a reactive mechanism. It does not help in creating reusable infrastructure templates.</p>

<p><strong>Attach an IAM policy to interns preventing them from creating an Amazon RDS database</strong> - Using an IAM policy to prevent interns from creating an Amazon RDS database does not solve the problem of allowing any user to create resources by leveraging reusable infrastructure templates. So, this option is ruled out.</p>

<p>References:</p>

<p><a href="https://aws.amazon.com/premiumsupport/technology/trusted-advisor/">https://aws.amazon.com/premiumsupport/technology/trusted-advisor/</a></p>

<p><a href="https://aws.amazon.com/cloudformation/">https://aws.amazon.com/cloudformation/</a></p>
</div></div><div data-purpose="domain-pane" class="domain-pane--domain-pane--Pw9dK"><div class="domain-pane--domain-pane-header--2263m ud-heading-md">Domain</div><div class="ud-text-md">Design High-Performing Architectures</div></div></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane-wrapper--2bGiz"><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane--sIcOh result-pane--accordion-panel--TEJg7"><div class="result-pane--question-header-wrapper--3DCpC"><div class="result-pane--question-header--pTUOx"><span class="result-pane--question-header-collapsed-text--WVdEr"><span class="result-pane--pane-title--f-2kd ud-heading-md"><span data-purpose="question-result-header-status-icon" class="result-pane--answer-status-icon--ebl6C"><span class="result-pane--question-icon-background--AskFJ" data-purpose="question-result-header-status-icon-background" style="background: oklch(0.7905 0.0283 281.19);"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-medium" style="color: oklch(0.7905 0.0283 281.19);"><use xlink:href="#icon-close"></use></svg></span></span><span>Question 28</span><span data-purpose="question-result-header-status-label" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);">Skipped</span><button type="button" class="ud-btn ud-btn-small ud-btn-link ud-btn-text-sm"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-xsmall ud-icon-color-info m"><use xlink:href="#icon-sparkles"></use></svg><span class="ud-btn-label">Explain this further</span></button></span><button type="button" class="ud-btn ud-btn-large ud-btn-ghost ud-btn-text-md ud-btn-icon ud-btn-icon-large"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-medium ud-icon-color-neutral"><use xlink:href="#icon-collapse"></use></svg></button></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="result-pane--question-format--PBvdY ud-text-md rt-scaffolding" id="question-prompt"><p>A company uses Application Load Balancers in multiple AWS Regions. The Application Load Balancers receive inconsistent traffic that varies throughout the year. The engineering team at the company needs to allow the IP addresses of the Application Load Balancers in the on-premises firewall to enable connectivity.</p>

<p>Which of the following represents the MOST scalable solution with minimal configuration changes?</p></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane-expanded-content--Og5Vc"><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-correct--PLOEU" data-purpose="answer"><div><span data-purpose="answer-result-header-user-label" class="result-pane--answer-by-user-label--PSH86 ud-heading-xs" style="background: oklch(0.8101 0.0873 162.22); color: oklch(0.3072 0.0555 158.67);">Correct answer</span></div><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.2565 0.0265 278.04);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Set up AWS Global Accelerator. Register the Application Load Balancers in different Regions to the AWS Global Accelerator. Configure the on-premises firewall's rule to allow static IP addresses associated with the AWS Global Accelerator</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Develop an AWS Lambda script to get the IP addresses of the Application Load Balancers in different Regions. Configure the on-premises firewall's rule to allow the IP addresses of the Application Load Balancers</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Set up a Network Load Balancer in one Region. Register the private IP addresses of the Application Load Balancers in different Regions with the Network Load Balancer. Configure the on-premises firewall's rule to allow the Elastic IP address attached to the Network Load Balancer</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Migrate all Application Load Balancers in different Regions to the Network Load Balancers. Configure the on-premises firewall's rule to allow the Elastic IP addresses of all the Network Load Balancers</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-related-fields--c3m--"><div class="overall-explanation-pane--overall-explanation--G-hLQ ud-form-group"><label class="ud-heading-md ud-form-label ud-heading-sm" for="form-group--1083">Overall explanation</label><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-text-md rt-scaffolding" id="overall-explanation"><p>Correct option:</p>

<p><strong>Set up AWS Global Accelerator. Register the Application Load Balancers in different Regions to the AWS Global Accelerator. Configure the on-premises firewall's rule to allow static IP addresses associated with the AWS Global Accelerator</strong></p>

<p>AWS Global Accelerator is a networking service that helps you improve the availability and performance of the applications that you offer to your global users. AWS Global Accelerator is easy to set up, configure, and manage. It provides static IP addresses that provide a fixed entry point to your applications and eliminate the complexity of managing specific IP addresses for different AWS Regions and Availability Zones.</p>

<p>Associate the static IP addresses provided by AWS Global Accelerator to regional AWS resources or endpoints, such as Network Load Balancers, Application Load Balancers, Amazon EC2 Instances, and Elastic IP addresses. The IP addresses are anycast from AWS edge locations so they provide onboarding to the AWS global network close to your users.</p>

<p>Simplified and resilient traffic routing for multi-Region applications using AWS Global Accelerator:
<img src="https://assets-pt.media.datacumulus.com/aws-saa-pt/assets/pt3-q58-i1.jpg" style="display: none;"><span class="ud-component--base-components--open-full-size-image"><div class="open-full-size-image--wrapper--R4gIm" data-purpose="open-full-size-image"><img src="https://assets-pt.media.datacumulus.com/aws-saa-pt/assets/pt3-q58-i1.jpg" alt="" loading="eager"><button type="button" class="ud-btn ud-btn-medium ud-btn-link ud-btn-text-sm open-full-size-image--backdrop--Zor3j"><svg aria-label="Larger image" role="img" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-large ud-icon-color-neutral"><use xlink:href="#icon-search"></use></svg></button></div></span>
via - <a href="https://aws.amazon.com/global-accelerator/">https://aws.amazon.com/global-accelerator/</a></p>

<p>Incorrect options:</p>

<p><strong>Migrate all Application Load Balancers in different Regions to the Network Load Balancers. Configure the on-premises firewall's rule to allow the Elastic IP addresses of all the Network Load Balancers</strong> - Although you could potentially migrate the Application Load Balancers to Network Load Balancers, this option requires changes to the on-premises firewall's configuration rules, hence this is not the right fit for the given use-case. It is more optimal to manage the two static IPs provided by the AWS Global Accelerator for configuring the firewall.</p>

<p><strong>Set up a Network Load Balancer in one Region. Register the private IP addresses of the Application Load Balancers in different Regions with the Network Load Balancer. Configure the on-premises firewall's rule to allow the Elastic IP address attached to the Network Load Balancer</strong> - Using a single Network Load Balancer is not possible across AWS regions since an Network Load Balancer is Region bound. Multiple Network Load Balancers have to be registered for the on-premises firewall.</p>

<p><strong>Develop an AWS Lambda script to get the IP addresses of the Application Load Balancers in different Regions. Configure the on-premises firewall's rule to allow the IP addresses of the Application Load Balancers</strong> - This option requires on-going changes to the on-premises firewall's configuration rules because the IP addresses of the Application Load Balancers would keep changing. Hence this is not the right fit for the given use-case. It is more optimal to configure the firewall with a one-time change for the two static IPs provided by the AWS Global Accelerator.</p>

<p>Reference:</p>

<p><a href="https://aws.amazon.com/global-accelerator/faqs/">https://aws.amazon.com/global-accelerator/faqs/</a></p>

data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="result-pane--question-format--PBvdY ud-text-md rt-scaffolding" id="question-prompt"><p>Amazon Route 53 is configured to route traffic to two Network Load Balancer nodes belonging to two Availability Zones (AZs): <code>AZ-A</code> and <code>AZ-B</code>. Cross-zone load balancing is disabled. <code>AZ-A</code> has four targets and <code>AZ-B</code> has six targets.</p>

<p>Which of the below statements is true about traffic distribution to the target instances from Amazon Route 53?</p></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane-expanded-content--Og5Vc"><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-correct--PLOEU" data-purpose="answer"><div><span data-purpose="answer-result-header-user-label" class="result-pane--answer-by-user-label--PSH86 ud-heading-xs" style="background: oklch(0.8101 0.0873 162.22); color: oklch(0.3072 0.0555 158.67);">Correct answer</span></div><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.2565 0.0265 278.04);"><use <code>AZ-A</code> receives 12.5% of the traffic</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Each of the six targets in <code>AZ-B</code> receives 10% of the traffic</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Each of the four targets in <code>AZ-A</code> receives 10% of the traffic</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Each of the four targets in <code>AZ-A</code> receives 8% of the traffic</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-related-fields--c3m--"><div class="overall-explanation-pane--overall-explanation--G-hLQ ud-form-group"><label class="ud-heading-md ud-form-label ud-heading-sm" for="form-group--1085">Overall explanation</label><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-text-md rt-scaffolding" id="overall-explanation"><p>Correct option:</p>

<p><strong>Each of the four targets in <code>AZ-A</code> receives 12.5% of the traffic</strong></p>

<p>The nodes for your load balancer distribute requests from clients to registered targets. When cross-zone load balancing is enabled, each load balancer node distributes traffic across the registered targets in all enabled Availability Zones (AZs). When cross-zone load balancing is disabled, each load balancer node distributes traffic only across the registered targets in its Availability Zone (AZ).</p>

<p>Amazon Route 53 will distribute traffic such that each load balancer node receives 50% of the traffic from the clients.</p>

<p>If cross-zone load balancing is disabled:
1. Each of the four targets in <code>AZ-A</code> receives 12.5% of the traffic.
2. Each of the six targets in <code>AZ-B</code> receives 8.3% of the traffic.</p>

<p>This is because each load balancer node can route its 50% of the client traffic only to targets in its Availability Zone (AZ).</p>

<p>Incorrect options:</p>

<p><strong>Each of the six targets in <code>AZ-B</code> receives 10% of the traffic</strong> - As mentioned above in the correct explanation, each of the six targets in <code>AZ-B</code> receives 8.3% of the traffic.</p>

<p><strong>Each of the four targets in <code>AZ-A</code> receives 8% of the traffic</strong> - As mentioned above in the correct explanation, each of the four targets in <code>AZ-A</code> receives 12.5% of the traffic.</p>

<p><strong>Each of the four targets in <code>AZ-A</code> receives 10% of the traffic</strong> - As mentioned above in the correct explanation, each of the four targets in <code>AZ-A</code> receives 12.5% of the traffic.</p>

<p>Reference:</p>

<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/elasticloadbalancing/latest/userguide/how-elastic-load-balancing-works.html">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/elasticloadbalancing/latest/userguide/how-elastic-load-balancing-works.html</a></p>

class="result-pane--question-header-collapsed-text--WVdEr"><span class="result-pane--pane-title--f-2kd ud-heading-md"><span data-purpose="question-result-header-status-icon" class="result-pane--answer-status-icon--ebl6C"><span class="result-pane--question-icon-background--AskFJ" data-purpose="question-result-header-status-icon-background" style="background: oklch(0.7905 ud-btn-icon-large"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-medium ud-icon-color-neutral"><use xlink:href="#icon-collapse"></use></svg></button></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="result-pane--question-format--PBvdY ud-text-md rt-scaffolding" id="question-prompt"><p>A company has developed a popular photo-sharing website using a serverless pattern on the AWS Cloud using Amazon API Gateway and AWS Lambda. The backend uses an Amazon RDS PostgreSQL database. The website is experiencing high read traffic and the AWS Lambda functions are putting an increased read load on the Amazon RDS database.</p>

<p>The architecture team is planning to increase the read throughput of the database, without changing the application's core logic. As a Solutions Architect, what do you recommend?</p></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane-expanded-content--Og5Vc"><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-correct--PLOEU" data-purpose="answer"><div><span data-purpose="answer-result-header-user-label" class="result-pane--answer-by-user-label--PSH86 ud-heading-xs" style="background: oklch(0.8101 0.0873 162.22); color: oklch(0.3072 0.0555 158.67);">Correct answer</span></div><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.2565 0.0265 278.04);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Use Amazon RDS Read Replicas</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Use Amazon DynamoDB</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Use Amazon ElastiCache</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Use Amazon RDS Multi-AZ feature</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-related-fields--c3m--"><div class="overall-explanation-pane--overall-explanation--G-hLQ ud-form-group"><label class="ud-heading-md ud-form-label ud-heading-sm" for="form-group--1087">Overall explanation</label><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-text-md rt-scaffolding" id="overall-explanation"><p>Correct option:</p>

<p><strong>Use Amazon RDS Read Replicas</strong></p>

<p>Amazon RDS Read Replicas provide enhanced performance and durability for RDS database (DB) instances. They make it easy to elastically scale out beyond the capacity constraints of a single DB instance for read-heavy database workloads. You can create one or more replicas of a given source DB Instance and serve high-volume application read traffic from multiple copies of your data, thereby increasing aggregate read throughput. Read replicas can also be promoted when needed to become standalone DB instances.</p>

<p>More on Amazon RDS Read Replicas:
<img src="https://assets-pt.media.datacumulus.com/aws-saa-pt/assets/pt3-q13-i1.jpg" style="display: none;"><span class="ud-component--base-components--open-full-size-image"><div class="open-full-size-image--wrapper--R4gIm" data-purpose="open-full-size-image"><img src="https://assets-pt.media.datacumulus.com/aws-saa-pt/assets/pt3-q13-i1.jpg" alt="" loading="eager"><button type="button" class="ud-btn ud-btn-medium ud-btn-link ud-btn-text-sm open-full-size-image--backdrop--Zor3j"><svg aria-label="Larger image" role="img" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-large ud-icon-color-neutral"><use xlink:href="#icon-search"></use></svg></button></div></span>
via - <a href="https://aws.amazon.com/rds/features/read-replicas/">https://aws.amazon.com/rds/features/read-replicas/</a></p>

<p>Incorrect options:</p>

<p><strong>Use Amazon RDS Multi-AZ feature</strong> - Amazon RDS Multi-AZ deployments provide enhanced availability and durability for RDS database (DB) instances, making them a natural fit for production database workloads. When you provision a Multi-AZ DB Instance, Amazon RDS automatically creates a primary DB Instance and synchronously replicates the data to a standby instance in a different Availability Zone (AZ). Each AZ runs on its own physically distinct, independent infrastructure, and is engineered to be highly reliable. In case of an infrastructure failure, Amazon RDS performs an automatic failover to the standby (or to a read replica in the case of Amazon Aurora), so that you can resume database operations as soon as the failover is complete.</p>

<p><strong>Use Amazon ElastiCache</strong> - Amazon ElastiCache allows you to seamlessly set up, run, and scale popular open-Source compatible in-memory data stores in the cloud. Build data-intensive apps or boost the performance of your existing databases by retrieving data from high throughput and low latency in-memory data stores. Amazon ElastiCache is a popular choice for real-time use cases like Caching, Session Stores, Gaming, Geospatial Services, Real-Time Analytics, and Queuing.</p>

<p><strong>Use Amazon DynamoDB</strong> - Amazon DynamoDB is a key-value and document database that delivers single-digit millisecond performance at any scale. It's a fully managed, multi-Region, multi-master, durable database with built-in security, backup and restore, and in-memory caching for internet-scale applications. Amazon DynamoDB can handle more than 10 trillion requests per day and can support peaks of more than 20 million requests per second.</p>

<p>Amazon RDS Multi-AZ helps with disaster recovery in case of an AZ failure. Amazon ElastiCache would definitely help with the read load, but would require a refactor of the application's core logic. Amazon DynamoDB with DAX would also probably help with the read load, but once again it would require a refactor of the application's core logic. Here, our only option to scale reads is to use Amazon RDS Read Replicas.</p>

<p>References:</p>

<p><a href="https://aws.amazon.com/rds/features/multi-az/">https://aws.amazon.com/rds/features/multi-az/</a></p>

</div></div><div data-purpose="domain-pane" class="domain-pane--domain-pane--Pw9dK"><div class="domain-pane--domain-pane-header--2263m ud-heading-md">Domain</div><div class="ud-text-md">Design Resilient Architectures</div></div></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane-wrapper--2bGiz"><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane--sIcOh result-pane--accordion-panel--TEJg7"><div class="result-pane--question-header-wrapper--3DCpC"><div class="result-pane--question-header--pTUOx"><span class="result-pane--question-header-collapsed-text--WVdEr"><span class="result-pane--pane-title--f-2kd ud-heading-md"><span data-purpose="question-result-header-status-icon" class="result-pane--answer-status-icon--ebl6C"><span class="result-pane--question-icon-background--AskFJ" data-purpose="question-result-header-status-icon-background" style="background: oklch(0.7905 0.0283 281.19);"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-medium" style="color: oklch(0.7905 0.0283 281.19);"><use xlink:href="#icon-close"></use></svg></span></span><span>Question 31</span><span data-purpose="question-result-header-status-label" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);">Skipped</span><button type="button" class="ud-btn ud-btn-small ud-btn-link ud-btn-text-sm"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-xsmall ud-icon-color-info m"><use xlink:href="#icon-sparkles"></use></svg><span class="ud-btn-label">Explain this further</span></button></span><button type="button" class="ud-btn ud-btn-large ud-btn-ghost ud-btn-text-md ud-btn-icon ud-btn-icon-large"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-medium ud-icon-color-neutral"><use xlink:href="#icon-collapse"></use></svg></button></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="result-pane--question-format--PBvdY ud-text-md rt-scaffolding" id="question-prompt"><p>A global pharmaceutical company operates a hybrid cloud network. Its primary AWS workloads run in the us-west-2 Region, connected to its on-premises data center via an AWS Direct Connect connection. After acquiring a biotech firm headquartered in Europe, the company must integrate the biotech’s workloads, which are hosted in several VPCs in the eu-central-1 Region and connected to the biotech's on-premises facility through a separate Direct Connect link. All CIDR blocks are non-overlapping, and the business requires full connectivity between both data centers and all VPCs across the two Regions. The company also wants a scalable solution that minimizes manual network configuration and long-term operational overhead.</p>

<p>Which solution will best meet these requirements?</p></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane-expanded-content--Og5Vc"><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Establish inter-Region VPC peering between each VPC in the us-west-2 and eu-central-1 Regions. Use static routing tables in each VPC to define peer relationships and enable cross-Region communication</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-correct--PLOEU" data-purpose="answer"><div><span data-purpose="answer-result-header-user-label" class="result-pane--answer-by-user-label--PSH86 ud-heading-xs" style="background: oklch(0.8101 0.0873 162.22); color: oklch(0.3072 0.0555 158.67);">Correct answer</span></div><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.2565 0.0265 278.04);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Connect both Direct Connect links to a shared Direct Connect gateway. Attach each Region's virtual private gateway (VGW) to the Direct Connect gateway, enabling transitive routing between the VPCs and the on-premises networks across Regions</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Create private VIFs (virtual interfaces) in each Region and associate them directly with foreign-region VPCs using routing table entries and BGP. Use VPC endpoints in each account to forward cross-Region traffic</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Deploy EC2-based VPN appliances in each VPC. Configure a full mesh VPN topology between all VPCs and data centers using CloudHub-style routing across Regions</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-related-fields--c3m--"><div class="overall-explanation-pane--overall-explanation--G-hLQ ud-form-group"><label class="ud-heading-md ud-form-label ud-heading-sm" for="form-group--1089">Overall explanation</label><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-text-md rt-scaffolding" id="overall-explanation"><p>Correct option:</p>

<p><strong>Connect both Direct Connect links to a shared Direct Connect gateway. Attach each Region's virtual private gateway (VGW) to the Direct Connect gateway, enabling transitive routing between the VPCs and the on-premises networks across Regions</strong></p>

<p>This is the best solution for interconnecting multiple VPCs across Regions and between on-premises data centers, while maintaining low operational overhead. A Direct Connect gateway is a global resource that allows VPCs in any AWS Region (except China) to connect to Direct Connect via virtual private gateways (VGWs). By connecting both Direct Connect links to the same DX gateway and associating the VGWs of all relevant VPCs, the company can enable transitive routing across Regions and between on-premises locations and VPCs — without setting up complex peering or custom VPN appliances.</p>

<p><img src="https://assets-pt.media.datacumulus.com/aws-saa-pt/assets/pt3-q7-i1.jpg" style="display: none;"><span class="ud-component--base-components--open-full-size-image"><div class="open-full-size-image--wrapper--R4gIm" data-purpose="open-full-size-image"><img src="https://assets-pt.media.datacumulus.com/aws-saa-pt/assets/pt3-q7-i1.jpg" alt="" loading="eager"><button type="button" class="ud-btn ud-btn-medium ud-btn-link ud-btn-text-sm open-full-size-image--backdrop--Zor3j"><svg aria-label="Larger image" role="img" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-large ud-icon-color-neutral"><use xlink:href="#icon-search"></use></svg></button></div></span>
via - <a href="https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/networking-and-content-delivery/hybrid-cloud-architectures-using-aws-direct-connect-gateway/">https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/networking-and-content-delivery/hybrid-cloud-architectures-using-aws-direct-connect-gateway/</a></p>

<p>Incorrect options:</p>

<p><strong>Establish inter-Region VPC peering between each VPC in the us-west-2 and eu-central-1 Regions. Use static routing tables in each VPC to define peer relationships and enable cross-Region communication</strong> - While inter-Region VPC peering does support direct communication between two VPCs, it does not provide transitive routing. That means each VPC must be peered individually, and on-prem connectivity cannot be transited through VPCs. Additionally, managing dozens of peering connections and route tables is not scalable as the number of VPCs grows.</p>

<p><strong>Deploy EC2-based VPN appliances in each VPC. Configure a full mesh VPN topology between all VPCs and data centers using CloudHub-style routing across Regions</strong> - While possible, deploying a full mesh VPN using EC2 instances or third-party VPN appliances introduces high operational complexity, including manual configuration, key management, and failure handling. CloudHub is only recommended when you have Site-to-Site VPNs connected to a single virtual private gateway, which is not scalable or efficient across multiple VPCs and Regions.</p>

<p><strong>Create private VIFs (virtual interfaces) in each Region and associate them directly with foreign-region VPCs using routing table entries and BGP. Use VPC endpoints in each account to forward cross-Region traffic</strong> - Private VIFs are used to connect a Direct Connect to a VGW or a transit gateway in the same Region. They cannot be directly associated with a foreign-region VPC. Furthermore, VPC endpoints are for accessing AWS services within a Region and cannot route private traffic between Regions. This design does not enable global hybrid connectivity.</p>

class="result-pane--answer-status-icon--ebl6C"><span class="result-pane--question-icon-background--AskFJ" data-purpose="question-result-header-status-icon-background" style="background: oklch(0.7905 xlink:href="#icon-close"></use></svg></span></span><span>Question 32</span><span data-purpose="question-result-header-status-label" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);">Skipped</span><button type="button" class="ud-btn ud-btn-small ud-btn-link ud-btn-text-sm"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-xsmall ud-icon-color-info m"><use xlink:href="#icon-sparkles"></use></svg><span class="ud-btn-label">Explain this further</span></button></span><button type="button" class="ud-btn ud-btn-large ud-btn-ghost ud-btn-text-md ud-btn-icon data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="result-pane--question-format--PBvdY ud-text-md rt-scaffolding" id="question-prompt"><p>The development team at a social media company wants to handle some complicated queries such as "What are the number of likes on the videos that have been posted by friends of a user A?".</p>

<p>As a solutions architect, which of the following AWS database services would you suggest as the BEST fit to handle such use cases?</p></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane-expanded-content--Og5Vc"><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Amazon OpenSearch Service</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Amazon Redshift</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-correct--PLOEU" data-purpose="answer"><div><span data-purpose="answer-result-header-user-label" class="result-pane--answer-by-user-label--PSH86 ud-heading-xs" style="background: oklch(0.8101 0.0873 162.22); color: oklch(0.3072 0.0555 158.67);">Correct answer</span></div><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.2565 0.0265 278.04);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Amazon Neptune</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Amazon Aurora</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-related-fields--c3m--"><div class="overall-explanation-pane--overall-explanation--G-hLQ ud-form-group"><label class="ud-heading-md ud-form-label ud-heading-sm" for="form-group--1091">Overall explanation</label><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-text-md rt-scaffolding" id="overall-explanation"><p>Correct option:</p>

<p><strong>Amazon Neptune</strong></p>

<p>Amazon Neptune is a fast, reliable, fully managed graph database service that makes it easy to build and run applications that work with highly connected datasets. The core of Amazon Neptune is a purpose-built, high-performance graph database engine optimized for storing billions of relationships and querying the graph with milliseconds latency. Neptune powers graph use cases such as recommendation engines, fraud detection, knowledge graphs, drug discovery, and network security.</p>

<p>Amazon Neptune is highly available, with read replicas, point-in-time recovery, continuous backup to Amazon S3, and replication across Availability Zones. Neptune is secure with support for HTTPS encrypted client connections and encryption at rest. Neptune is fully managed, so you no longer need to worry about database management tasks such as hardware provisioning, software patching, setup, configuration, or backups.</p>

<p>Amazon Neptune can quickly and easily process large sets of user-profiles and interactions to build social networking applications. Neptune enables highly interactive graph queries with high throughput to bring social features into your applications. For example, if you are building a social feed into your application, you can use Neptune to provide results that prioritize showing your users the latest updates from their family, from friends whose updates they ‘Like,’ and from friends who live close to them.</p>

<p>Social Networking example with Amazon Neptune:
<img src="https://assets-pt.media.datacumulus.com/aws-saa-pt/assets/pt3-q11-i1.jpg" style="display: none;"><span class="ud-component--base-components--open-full-size-image"><div class="open-full-size-image--wrapper--R4gIm" data-purpose="open-full-size-image"><img src="https://assets-pt.media.datacumulus.com/aws-saa-pt/assets/pt3-q11-i1.jpg" alt="" loading="eager"><button type="button" class="ud-btn ud-btn-medium ud-btn-link ud-btn-text-sm open-full-size-image--backdrop--Zor3j"><svg aria-label="Larger image" role="img" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-large ud-icon-color-neutral"><use xlink:href="#icon-search"></use></svg></button></div></span>
via - <a href="https://aws.amazon.com/neptune/">https://aws.amazon.com/neptune/</a></p>

<p>Identity graphs example with Amazon Neptune:
<img src="https://assets-pt.media.datacumulus.com/aws-saa-pt/assets/pt3-q11-i2.jpg" style="display: none;"><span class="ud-component--base-components--open-full-size-image"><div class="open-full-size-image--wrapper--R4gIm" data-purpose="open-full-size-image"><img src="https://assets-pt.media.datacumulus.com/aws-saa-pt/assets/pt3-q11-i2.jpg" alt="" loading="eager"><button type="button" class="ud-btn ud-btn-medium ud-btn-link ud-btn-text-sm open-full-size-image--backdrop--Zor3j"><svg aria-label="Larger image" role="img" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-large ud-icon-color-neutral"><use xlink:href="#icon-search"></use></svg></button></div></span>
via - <a href="https://aws.amazon.com/neptune/">https://aws.amazon.com/neptune/</a></p>

<p>Incorrect options:</p>

<p><strong>Amazon OpenSearch Service</strong> - Amazon OpenSearch Service is a managed service that makes it easy for you to perform interactive log analytics, real-time application monitoring, website search, and more. OpenSearch is an open source, distributed search and analytics suite derived from Elasticsearch. Amazon OpenSearch Service offers the latest versions of OpenSearch, support for 19 versions of Elasticsearch (1.5 to 7.10 versions), as well as visualization capabilities powered by OpenSearch Dashboards and Kibana (1.5 to 7.10 versions). Amazon OpenSearch Service currently has tens of thousands of active customers with hundreds of thousands of clusters under management processing trillions of requests per month.</p>

<p><strong>Amazon Redshift</strong> - Amazon Redshift is a fully-managed petabyte-scale cloud-based data warehouse product designed for large scale data set storage and analysis. The given use-case is not about data warehousing, so this is not a correct option.</p>

<p><strong>Amazon Aurora</strong> - Amazon Aurora is a MySQL and PostgreSQL-compatible relational database built for the cloud, that combines the performance and availability of traditional enterprise databases with the simplicity and cost-effectiveness of open source databases. Amazon Aurora features a distributed, fault-tolerant, self-healing storage system that auto-scales up to 64 terabytes per database instance. Aurora is not an in-memory database. Here, we need a graph database due to the highly connected datasets and queries, therefore Neptune is the best answer.</p>

<p>Reference:</p>

<p><a href="https://aws.amazon.com/neptune/">https://aws.amazon.com/neptune/</a></p>

High-Performing Architectures</div></div></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane-wrapper--2bGiz"><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane--sIcOh result-pane--accordion-panel--TEJg7"><div class="result-pane--question-header-wrapper--3DCpC"><div class="result-pane--question-header--pTUOx"><span class="result-pane--question-header-collapsed-text--WVdEr"><span class="result-pane--pane-title--f-2kd ud-heading-md"><span data-purpose="question-result-header-status-icon" class="result-pane--answer-status-icon--ebl6C"><span class="result-pane--question-icon-background--AskFJ" data-purpose="question-result-header-status-icon-background" style="background: oklch(0.7905 0.0283 281.19);"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-medium" style="color: oklch(0.7905 0.0283 281.19);"><use xlink:href="#icon-close"></use></svg></span></span><span>Question 33</span><span data-purpose="question-result-header-status-label" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);">Skipped</span><button type="button" class="ud-btn ud-btn-small ud-btn-link ud-btn-text-sm"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-xsmall ud-icon-color-info m"><use xlink:href="#icon-sparkles"></use></svg><span class="ud-btn-label">Explain this further</span></button></span><button type="button" class="ud-btn ud-btn-large ud-btn-ghost ud-btn-text-md ud-btn-icon ud-btn-icon-large"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-medium ud-icon-color-neutral"><use xlink:href="#icon-collapse"></use></svg></button></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="result-pane--question-format--PBvdY ud-text-md rt-scaffolding" id="question-prompt"><p>A company has noticed that its Amazon EBS Elastic Volume (io1) accounts for 90% of the cost and the remaining 10% cost can be attributed to the Amazon EC2 instance. The Amazon CloudWatch metrics report that both the Amazon EC2 instance and the Amazon EBS volume are under-utilized. The Amazon CloudWatch metrics also show that the Amazon EBS volume has occasional I/O bursts. The entire infrastructure is managed by AWS CloudFormation.</p>

<p>As a Solutions Architect, what do you propose to reduce the costs?</p></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane-expanded-content--Og5Vc"><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Change the Amazon EC2 instance type to something much smaller</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Keep the Amazon EBS volume to io1 and reduce the IOPS</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-correct--PLOEU" data-purpose="answer"><div><span data-purpose="answer-result-header-user-label" class="result-pane--answer-by-user-label--PSH86 ud-heading-xs" style="background: oklch(0.8101 0.0873 162.22); color: oklch(0.3072 0.0555 158.67);">Correct answer</span></div><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.2565 0.0265 278.04);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Convert the Amazon EC2 instance EBS volume to gp2</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Don't use a AWS CloudFormation template to create the database as the AWS CloudFormation service incurs greater service charges</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-related-fields--c3m--"><div class="overall-explanation-pane--overall-explanation--G-hLQ ud-form-group"><label class="ud-heading-md ud-form-label ud-heading-sm" for="form-group--1093">Overall explanation</label><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-text-md rt-scaffolding" id="overall-explanation"><p>Correct option:</p>

<p>Amazon EBS provides the various volume types, that differ in performance characteristics and price so that you can tailor your storage performance and cost to the needs of your applications. The volumes types fall into two categories:</p>

<p>SSD-backed volumes optimized for transactional workloads involving frequent read/write operations with small I/O size, where the dominant performance attribute is IOPS.</p>

<p>HDD-backed volumes optimized for large streaming workloads where throughput (measured in MiB/s) is a better performance measure than IOPS</p>

<p>Provisioned IOPS SSD (io1) volumes are designed to meet the needs of I/O-intensive workloads, particularly database workloads, that are sensitive to storage performance and consistency. Unlike gp2, which uses a bucket and credit model to calculate performance, an io1 volume allows you to specify a consistent IOPS rate when you create the volume, and Amazon EBS delivers the provisioned performance 99.9 percent of the time.</p>

<p><strong>Convert the Amazon EC2 instance EBS volume to gp2</strong></p>

<p>General Purpose SSD (gp2) volumes offer cost-effective storage that is ideal for a broad range of workloads. These volumes deliver single-digit millisecond latencies and the ability to burst to 3,000 IOPS for an extended duration. Between a minimum of 100 IOPS (at 33.33 GiB and below) and a maximum of 16,000 IOPS (at 5,334 GiB and above), baseline performance scales linearly at 3 IOPS per GiB of volume size. AWS designs gp2 volumes to deliver a provisioned performance of 99% uptime. A gp2 volume can range in size from 1 GiB to 16 TiB.</p>

<p>Therefore, gp2 is the right choice as it is more cost-effective than io1, and it also allows a burst in performance when needed.</p>

<p>Incorrect options:</p>

<p><strong>Keep the Amazon EBS volume to io1 and reduce the IOPS</strong> - Keeping the Amazon EBS volume to io1 and reducing the IOPS may interfere with the burst of performance we need, so this option is ruled out.</p>

<p><strong>Change the Amazon EC2 instance type to something much smaller</strong> - Changing the Amazon EC2 instance type to something much smaller won't affect 90% of the costs that are incurred, therefore this option is also incorrect.</p>

<p><strong>Don't use a AWS CloudFormation template to create the database as the AWS CloudFormation service incurs greater service charges</strong> - This statement is incorrect as AWS CloudFormation is a free service to use. The resources that are invoked by CloudFormation are charged as per their utilization rates, but using AWS CloudFormation will not cost anything.</p>

<p>References:</p>

<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AWSEC2/latest/UserGuide/ebs-volume-types.html#EBSVolumeTypes_gp2">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AWSEC2/latest/UserGuide/ebs-volume-types.html#EBSVolumeTypes_gp2</a></p>

<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AWSEC2/latest/UserGuide/ebs-volume-types.html#EBSVolumeTypes_piops">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AWSEC2/latest/UserGuide/ebs-volume-types.html#EBSVolumeTypes_piops</a></p>
</div></div><div data-purpose="domain-pane" class="domain-pane--domain-pane--Pw9dK"><div class="domain-pane--domain-pane-header--2263m ud-heading-md">Domain</div><div class="ud-text-md">Design Cost-Optimized Architectures</div></div></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane-wrapper--2bGiz"><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane--sIcOh result-pane--accordion-panel--TEJg7"><div class="result-pane--question-header-wrapper--3DCpC"><div class="result-pane--question-header--pTUOx"><span class="result-pane--question-header-collapsed-text--WVdEr"><span class="result-pane--pane-title--f-2kd ud-heading-md"><span data-purpose="question-result-header-status-icon" class="result-pane--answer-status-icon--ebl6C"><span class="result-pane--question-icon-background--AskFJ" data-purpose="question-result-header-status-icon-background" style="background: oklch(0.7905 0.0283 281.19);"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-medium" style="color: oklch(0.7905 0.0283 281.19);"><use xlink:href="#icon-close"></use></svg></span></span><span>Question 34</span><span data-purpose="question-result-header-status-label" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);">Skipped</span><button type="button" class="ud-btn ud-btn-small ud-btn-link ud-btn-text-sm"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-xsmall ud-icon-color-info m"><use xlink:href="#icon-sparkles"></use></svg><span class="ud-btn-label">Explain this further</span></button></span><button type="button" class="ud-btn ud-btn-large ud-btn-ghost ud-btn-text-md ud-btn-icon ud-btn-icon-large"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-medium ud-icon-color-neutral"><use xlink:href="#icon-collapse"></use></svg></button></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="result-pane--question-format--PBvdY ud-text-md rt-scaffolding" id="question-prompt"><p>As a solutions architect, you have created a solution that utilizes an Application Load Balancer with stickiness and an Auto Scaling Group (ASG). The Auto Scaling Group spans across 2 Availability Zones (AZs). <code>AZ-A</code> has 3 Amazon EC2 instances and <code>AZ-B</code> has 4 Amazon EC2 instances. The Auto Scaling Group is about to go into a scale-in event due to the triggering of a Amazon CloudWatch alarm.</p>

<p>What will happen under the default Auto Scaling Group configuration?</p></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane-expanded-content--Og5Vc"><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>A random instance in the <code>AZ-A</code> will be terminated</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>A random instance will be terminated in <code>AZ-B</code></p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>An instance in the <code>AZ-A</code> will be created</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-correct--PLOEU" data-purpose="answer"><div><span data-purpose="answer-result-header-user-label" class="result-pane--answer-by-user-label--PSH86 ud-heading-xs" style="background: oklch(0.8101 0.0873 162.22); color: oklch(0.3072 0.0555 158.67);">Correct answer</span></div><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.2565 0.0265 278.04);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>The instance with the oldest launch template or launch configuration will be terminated in <code>AZ-B</code></p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-related-fields--c3m--"><div class="overall-explanation-pane--overall-explanation--G-hLQ ud-form-group"><label class="ud-heading-md ud-form-label ud-heading-sm" for="form-group--1095">Overall explanation</label><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-text-md rt-scaffolding" id="overall-explanation"><p>Correct option:</p>

<p><strong>The instance with the oldest launch template or launch configuration will be terminated in <code>AZ-B</code></strong></p>

<p>Amazon EC2 Auto Scaling helps you ensure that you have the correct number of Amazon EC2 instances available to handle the load for your application. You create collections of Amazon EC2 instances, called Auto Scaling groups. You can specify the minimum number of instances in each Auto Scaling group, and Amazon EC2 Auto Scaling ensures that your group never goes below this size.</p>

<p>With each Auto Scaling group, you can control when it adds instances (referred to as scaling out) or removes instances (referred to as scaling in) from your network architecture.</p>

<p>The default termination policy is designed to help ensure that your instances span Availability Zones evenly for high availability. The default policy is kept generic and flexible to cover a range of scenarios.</p>

<p>The default termination policy behavior is as follows:
1. Determine which Availability Zones (Azs) have the most instances and at least one instance that is not protected from scale-in.
2. Determine which instances to terminate to align the remaining instances to the allocation strategy for the On-Demand or Spot Instance that is terminating.
3. Determine whether any of the instances use the oldest launch template or configuration:
    3.a. Determine whether any of the instances use the oldest launch template unless there are instances that use a launch configuration.
    3.b. Determine whether any of the instances use the oldest launch configuration.
4. After applying all of the above criteria, if there are multiple unprotected instances to terminate, determine which instances are closest to the next billing hour.</p>

<p>Per the given use-case, AZs will be balanced first, then the instance with the oldest launch template or launch configuration within the applicable AZ (<code>AZ-B</code>) will be terminated.</p>

<p>Default Termination policy:
<img src="https://assets-pt.media.datacumulus.com/aws-saa-pt/assets/pt3-q16-i1.jpg" style="display: none;"><span class="ud-component--base-components--open-full-size-image"><div class="open-full-size-image--wrapper--R4gIm" data-purpose="open-full-size-image"><img src="https://assets-pt.media.datacumulus.com/aws-saa-pt/assets/pt3-q16-i1.jpg" alt="" loading="eager"><button type="button" class="ud-btn ud-btn-medium ud-btn-link ud-btn-text-sm open-full-size-image--backdrop--Zor3j"><svg aria-label="Larger image" role="img" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-large ud-icon-color-neutral"><use xlink:href="#icon-search"></use></svg></button></div></span>
via - <a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/autoscaling/ec2/userguide/as-instance-termination.html">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/autoscaling/ec2/userguide/as-instance-termination.html</a></p>

<p>Incorrect options:</p>

<p><strong>A random instance in the <code>AZ-A</code> will be terminated</strong></p>

<p><strong>An instance in the <code>AZ-A</code> will be created</strong></p>

<p><strong>A random instance will be terminated in <code>AZ-B</code></strong></p>

<p>These three options contradict the details provided in the explanation above. Hence these are incorrect.</p>

<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/autoscaling/ec2/userguide/as-instance-termination.html">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/autoscaling/ec2/userguide/as-instance-termination.html</a></p>

Resilient Architectures</div></div></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane-wrapper--2bGiz"><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane--sIcOh result-pane--accordion-panel--TEJg7"><div class="result-pane--question-header-wrapper--3DCpC"><div class="result-pane--question-header--pTUOx"><span class="result-pane--question-header-collapsed-text--WVdEr"><span class="result-pane--pane-title--f-2kd ud-heading-md"><span data-purpose="question-result-header-status-icon" class="result-pane--answer-status-icon--ebl6C"><span class="result-pane--question-icon-background--AskFJ" data-purpose="question-result-header-status-icon-background" style="background: oklch(0.7905 0.0283 281.19);"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-medium" style="color: oklch(0.7905 0.0283 281.19);"><use xlink:href="#icon-close"></use></svg></span></span><span>Question 35</span><span data-purpose="question-result-header-status-label" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);">Skipped</span><button type="button" class="ud-btn ud-btn-small ud-btn-link ud-btn-text-sm"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-xsmall ud-icon-color-info m"><use xlink:href="#icon-sparkles"></use></svg><span class="ud-btn-label">Explain this further</span></button></span><button type="button" class="ud-btn ud-btn-large ud-btn-ghost ud-btn-text-md ud-btn-icon ud-btn-icon-large"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-medium ud-icon-color-neutral"><use xlink:href="#icon-collapse"></use></svg></button></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="result-pane--question-format--PBvdY ud-text-md rt-scaffolding" id="question-prompt"><p>You are working for a software as a service (SaaS) company as a solutions architect and help design solutions for the company's customers. One of the customers is a bank and has a requirement to whitelist a public IP when the bank is accessing external services across the internet.</p>

<p>Which architectural choice do you recommend to maintain high availability, support scaling-up to 10 instances and comply with the bank's requirements?</p></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane-expanded-content--Og5Vc"><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Use a Classic Load Balancer with an Auto Scaling Group</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Use an Application Load Balancer with an Auto Scaling Group</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-correct--PLOEU" data-purpose="answer"><div><span data-purpose="answer-result-header-user-label" class="result-pane--answer-by-user-label--PSH86 ud-heading-xs" style="background: oklch(0.8101 0.0873 162.22); color: oklch(0.3072 0.0555 158.67);">Correct answer</span></div><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.2565 0.0265 278.04);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Use a Network Load Balancer with an Auto Scaling Group</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Use an Auto Scaling Group with Dynamic Elastic IPs attachment</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-related-fields--c3m--"><div class="overall-explanation-pane--overall-explanation--G-hLQ ud-form-group"><label class="ud-heading-md ud-form-label ud-heading-sm" for="form-group--1097">Overall explanation</label><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-text-md rt-scaffolding" id="overall-explanation"><p>Correct option:</p>

<p><strong>Use a Network Load Balancer with an Auto Scaling Group</strong></p>

<p>Network Load Balancer is best suited for use-cases involving low latency and high throughput workloads that involve scaling to millions of requests per second. Network Load Balancer operates at the connection level (Layer 4), routing connections to targets - Amazon EC2 instances, microservices, and containers – within Amazon Virtual Private Cloud (Amazon VPC) based on IP protocol data. A Network Load Balancer functions at the fourth layer of the Open Systems Interconnection (OSI) model. It can handle millions of requests per second.</p>

<p>Network Load Balancers expose a fixed IP to the public web, therefore allowing your application to be predictably reached using this IP, while allowing you to scale your application behind the Network Load Balancer using an ASG.</p>

<p>Incorrect options:</p>

<p>Classic Load Balancers and Application Load Balancers use the private IP addresses associated with their Elastic network interfaces as the source IP address for requests forwarded to your web servers.</p>

<p>These IP addresses can be used for various purposes, such as allowing the load balancer traffic on the web servers and for request processing. It's a best practice to use security group referencing on the web servers for whitelisting load balancer traffic from Classic Load Balancers or Application Load Balancers.</p>

<p>However, because Network Load Balancers don't support security groups, based on the target group configurations, the IP addresses of the clients or the private IP addresses associated with the Network Load Balancers must be allowed on the web server's security group.</p>

<p><strong>Use a Classic Load Balancer with an Auto Scaling Group</strong> - Classic Load Balancer provides basic load balancing across multiple Amazon EC2 instances and operates at both the request level and connection level. Classic Load Balancer is intended for applications that were built within the Amazon EC2-Classic network.</p>

<p><strong>Use an Application Load Balancer with an Auto Scaling Group</strong> - Application Load Balancer operates at the request level (layer 7), routing traffic to targets – Amazon EC2 instances, containers, IP addresses and AWS Lambda functions based on the content of the request. Ideal for advanced load balancing of HTTP and HTTPS traffic, Application Load Balancer provides advanced request routing targeted at the delivery of modern application architectures, including microservices and container-based applications.</p>

<p>Application and Classic Load Balancers expose a fixed DNS (=URL) rather than the IP address. So these are incorrect options for the given use-case.</p>

<p><strong>Use an Auto Scaling Group with Dynamic Elastic IPs attachment</strong> - The option "Use an Auto Scaling Group (ASG) with Dynamic Elastic IPs attachment" has been added as a distractor. ASG does not have a dynamic Elastic IPs attachment feature.</p>
